The coal and instrument industry association sent a letter requesting a reduction in coal taxes and permission to lift the seal to alleviate business difficulties. The decision was to investigate the case and submit it to the meeting for review and action.

Robbery Case Reported to the Bureau, Complicated Inside Story Hu Xianchu, a partner in the Senshengqiao cottonseed oil cake shop outside the north gate, went to Shanghai the day before yesterday to collect 1,950 yuan in oil payments from the Yuanda Oil Shop. He took the night express train back to Wuxi, and after getting off the train, he took a streetcar back to the shop to report his return. Unexpectedly, as soon as Hu entered the shop, he suddenly became flustered, his face pale. He told Manager Wang Shufan that after collecting the payment in Shanghai and returning to Wuxi, he took a streetcar to return to the shop to hand in the payment. Unexpectedly, when passing the Jiyu School along the Dahe Pond, he was suddenly met by three bandits who robbed him of the entire payment, as well as three velvet hats, a pair of shoes, and a cat fur robe. The bandits fled in the direction of the Zhuzilong alley. After hearing this, Wang Shufan immediately ordered Xianchu to report to the Fifth Branch of the Public Security Bureau, which had jurisdiction over the area. After receiving the report, Chief Peng of the branch sent officers and police to investigate the scene of the incident, but they found no clues. They returned to the bureau to report their findings. However, according to outside rumors, the inside story of this case is complicated, and there must be other reasons.

General Order to All Counties to Strictly Arrest Bureau Members Hua Pu, the director of the County Public Security Bureau of this county, reported that Huang Bingjian, a member of the 16th Branch of the Public Security Bureau in Anzhen, District 8, had privately concealed opium, bribed and exchanged opium offenders, and abandoned his post and fled without a trace. Yesterday, he specially submitted a request to the County Government, requesting that it be forwarded to the Department of Civil Affairs, allowing all counties to be notified to strictly arrest him, bring him to justice, and try him.

Changzhou 85

Temporary Court Opens for Trial of Riot Case The County Government organized a temporary court to try the riot case that occurred in Wuyi County on October 18th. The trial opened at 1 PM on the 21st, with County Magistrate Zhang Peng as the presiding judge and Huang Jingbai and Liu Jinyong as the judges. The courtroom was extremely crowded with spectators. First, the victim, Lu Zao, testified about the circumstances of the assault and witnessed Jin Xiangsheng assaulting Wu Wenbi. Next, the defendants, Guo Junfu, chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and Ye Jinde, Zhang Chengguan, Xu Cixiong, Zhang Guangyao, Li Ziying, Zhang Jinrong, and Jin Xiangsheng, were questioned. Guo Junfu testified that he was forced to petition at the time. Ye Jinde and the others all denied participating in the riot. Next, the witnesses Zhu Songnian, Yang Yin, Yang Menglong, Liu Jun, and Qian Runzhi were questioned. Some testified about the riotous behavior, while others testified that Jin Xiangsheng was indeed the murderer. Later, the victim, Lu Zao, identified Ye Jinde as the assailant who hit him. As a result, Guo Junfu was released on bail, while Ye Jinde and the others were returned to custody, and the witnesses were dismissed.

Bandit Den Cracked at the Border of Wu and Cheng The Xuejiatou Village, located at the border of Wu and Cheng counties, was raided by the nearby self-defense corps. Two bandits, Xue Sanheshang and Xue Kunda, were captured at the home of Xue Sanheshang, and the hostage, Cai Shusheng, was rescued. However, the gardener was shot twice by the bandit guarding the hostage, and the bandit escaped. The bandits were handed over to Jiangyin for trial on the 22nd.

Nantong 86

Incineration of Opium Case to be Tried in Zhenjiang The Nantong County Court incinerated opium and discovered that more than two thousand taels were missing or counterfeit. The High Court ordered the Zhenjiang District Court to investigate thoroughly. Prosecutor Yan Chang has come to Tong to investigate. It is now known that this case will be tried in Zhenjiang, where relevant witnesses will be summoned for questioning.

Investigation of Gunfire from Gunboat The Provincial Government telegraphed the County Government, ordering an investigation of the gunboat that sailed from Tong to Bailonggang on the Yangtze River on the 16th and fired machine guns. County Magistrate Zhang has requested the garrison troops along the Yangtze River to investigate.

Yuxi Mang Cao Branch Robbed The Yuxi Mang Cao branch was suddenly robbed, resulting in significant losses. Grain certificates from the 16th to the 20th year were also stolen. The County Government has sent a commissioner to investigate.

Rugao 87

Deputy Township Chief Shot and Killed by Bandits Chen Linwen, the deputy township chief of Muhu Township in the Lugang district, was attacked by a group of bandits at his home the day before yesterday at night. Three of the bandits carried pistols. After a thorough search and robbery, they hung Chen from a beam and shot him to death before leaving with a yell.

Jiangyin 88

Wheel Industry Association Petitions for Dredging the River The river from Jiuli River to Qingyang Sihe Gate is narrow. Every winter, the river water is shallow and dry, and bamboo rafts and heavily loaded coal boats are congested. This year's flood caused a disaster, and the banks collapsed, raising the riverbed. The tide is also small, and the traffic of Chengxi small ferries is obstructed. The Wheel Industry Association specially presented a request to the Chamber of Commerce, which was forwarded to the county government, requesting that bamboo and wood rafts be reorganized to be smaller, and heavily loaded coal boats exceeding 3,000 tons be ordered to be unloaded. The chiefs of the 1st and 11th districts were ordered to send personnel to supervise the reorganization and unloading nearby. The Qingyang two public security branches outside the north were ordered to send police to assist in maintaining waterway traffic.

Zhenjiang 89

Financial Panic Trends Towards Stability The Jiangsu Provincial Government, due to the stagnation of Zhenjiang's finances, specially ordered the Department of Industry, together with the Departments of Civil Affairs and Finance, to convene the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce and the Zanqian Industry Association to hold a meeting in the meeting room of the Department yesterday afternoon at 2 PM. After discussion, it was decided that in addition to the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce, together with the Zanqian industries, continuing to have appropriate measures, in order to consolidate the city's financial situation, the three departments of Civil Affairs, Finance, and Industry would submit a proposal to the Provincial Government Committee to request the allocation of one million yuan from the existing construction bonds to be entrusted to the Chamber of Commerce for proper adjustment. This bond will be due in five months, and the Chamber of Commerce will be responsible for repayment. With this assistance, Zhenjiang's finances will become more stable.

Autocratic Marriage Sacrifices Young Girl Qiu Fu, a tailor near Lion Mountain in this city, has a daughter who is now nineteen years old and quite beautiful. She was betrothed to a Hang surnamed son from the southern township when she was a baby. However, the Hang son is by nature frivolous, and the girl does not care for him. She asked her parents for a divorce, but Qiu, greedy for Hang's wealth, did not allow a divorce. He recently decided to marry her off on the 25th of this month. Upon hearing this news, the girl secretly took opium last night until her family discovered it, but it was too late to save her. The Hang family is reportedly planning to file a lawsuit.

Money Collected, Robbed on the Way Gao Tinglong, who runs a grocery store on Xinma Road in this city, went to the southern township at 9 AM yesterday to collect debts because the end of the year was approaching. On his way home at 4 PM, while passing behind Wuli Mountain, he was suddenly chased by three bandits who shouted for him to stop. They tied Gao's hands and robbed him of the seventeen yuan he had collected, as well as twelve thousand copper coins in a sack.

Post Office Two Captains Clash, Transferred to Court Zhang Peifu, the captain of the Gaoyou County Police Team, and Xia Yuanhu, the captain of the Patrol Water Team, accused each other of being suspected of communicating with bandits. The Department of Civil Affairs ordered Cheng Zhuang, the chief of the Fifth Water Police District, to take a warship and arrest both Zhang and Xia. They arrived in the province on the 14th and were temporarily detained in the company headquarters of the Special Operations Battalion. On the 20th, they were transferred to the Zhenjiang District Court. After questioning by the prosecutor of the court, each was released on bail with 200 yuan in cash and a reliable shop guarantee, pending investigation and handling.

International Engineering Experts Inspect the Huai River Situation The Preparatory Office of the National Economic Commission, because international engineering experts have been invited to China to inspect the Huai River, specially telegraphed the governments of Anhui and Jiangsu provinces, ordering the county magistrates along the way to protect them when the time comes. It is now known that Mr. Haas, head of the Transportation and Communications Group of the League of Nations, will also participate in the inspection and study of various projects, starting with the inspection of the Huai River and departing soon.

Gaoyou 90

Salt Transportation Boat Robbed of Huge Sum According to a visitor from Xinghua, a salt transportation boat sailing from Yancheng to Xinghua the day before yesterday was suddenly met by seven or eight bandits in the middle of the journey. Each bandit carried a firearm and ordered the boat to dock. They swarmed aboard and robbed the boat of 13,500 yuan in silver dollars and banknotes before leaving with a yell.

Huzhou 91

Nanshuanlin Town Completely Looted by Bandits Nanshuanlin Town, located in the southern part of Huzhou, is situated between important towns such as Linghu and Xiaang. The town has more than 30 stores, and many residents are wealthy. Unexpectedly, at 7:30 PM on the 17th, six or seven bandit boats suddenly arrived with about 50 bandits. Holding quick-firing guns and wooden-cased guns, and speaking mostly in Henan accent, they swarmed ashore. Other bandits guarded the entrance to the town. The bandits fired more than ten shots and then proceeded to search each store in turn. After an hour, they fired shots and boarded their original boats to leave. It is now known that more than 20 stores were looted, including Hongtai General Merchandise Store, Chen Risheng Tobacco Store, Zhunfeng Grain Store, Fan Futai Beijing Goods Store, and Chen Xiongji Grocery Store, with losses exceeding one thousand yuan in silver dollars. Uncounted items. It is also heard that before the bandits looted the town, they broke into the home of Xin Haishan, a resident of Chejiatian, near the town, and robbed him of all his clothes and more than 600 yuan in cash, and kidnapped Xin Haishan onto their boat. Afterwards, Pan Shuren, the director of the Wuxing County Public Security Bureau in this city, went to Nanshuanlin to investigate the day before yesterday.

Ningbo 92

Zhenning Fishing Boat Confirmed to Have Sunk off Maou Zui The Zhenning fishing boat of the Zhengsheng Fishing Boat Bureau on the north bank of Yongbu River sailed out of Yong to fish on the 19th of last month, but has not been seen since. It has been rumored that the boat sank long ago. The bureau was deeply worried about the boat's long absence and sent someone to investigate the day before yesterday. It is now known that the investigators returned to Yong yesterday. The boat did sink off the coast of Mao Zui at about 11 AM on the 19th of last month due to a strong storm. No one witnessed it. All the personnel on the boat, such as boat owner Wu Gaofa (Dinghai native), chief mate Chen Chengyou (Dinghai native), chief engineer Chen Wenxing (Yinxian native), second engineer Tang Azhi (Jiangsu Nanhui native), and twenty-one others, all drowned with the boat. None survived. Boat owner Wu Gaofa lived in Li Qibao's house in Yangguan Nong on the north bank of Yongbu River and had three young children. After hearing the news, the families of the victims rushed to the bureau to cry and make a scene. The bureau is now discussing how to deal with the aftermath. It is also heard that the boat was not insured and the loss is over 70,000 to 80,000 yuan.

Hefei 93

Sixian Case Urgently Impacts Hefei's Defense Since the red bandits on the west bank of the Liu'an Pihe River were repeatedly attacked by Commander Yue's troops, their strength has been greatly damaged, and they have not dared to invade eastward for several months. Unexpectedly, this time, the red bandits in eastern Hubei were severely attacked by the Hubei provincial army and fled east to Yinghuo, causing the red bandits in the western part of Liu'an to suddenly grow in strength. On the 16th, they shelled Liu City from the west bank of the Pihe River and attacked from the Sujiabu area upstream. Commander Yue sent Wang Ducheng's brigade to engage them head-on. It is heard that they were repelled on the 17th. However, Commander Yue, believing that the number of bandits was very large, telegraphed the province for reinforcements. Commander-in-Chief Chen immediately ordered the 57th Division stationed in the Jiaohu area to rush to suppress them day and night. They will pass through Fei and go to Liu within a few days. County Magistrate Zhu Ting of Hefei, realizing that Heliu is in close proximity, and that absurd leaflets of the red bandits have recently appeared in the city, believes that the city's defense should be cautious. On the 17th, he convened a security meeting and decided to organize a temporary city defense office. He appointed 59 committee members from various public organizations and gentry, as well as military, political, party, and police agencies as ex-officio members. The city's security is being seriously searched by the 46th Division, together with the self-defense corps and police, to inspect the city gates, check household registrations, and inspect inns and hotels to prevent traitors from mixing in. On the afternoon of the 17th, County Magistrate Zhu sent the self-defense corps, public security team, and police team to temporarily inspect pedestrians at storytelling and entertainment venues such as the Wanshou Palace in the prefectural school, and sounded gongs throughout the city, requiring all households to place vats filled with clear water in front of their doors to prevent hidden dangers. He also telegraphed County Magistrate Wang Peishi of Shouxian, requesting that he implement joint defense and send troops to join forces at Wushan Temple in Yuji to suppress the bandits. Early in the morning of the 18th, the 46th Division sent 12 cars loaded with military supplies to Liu for replenishment. Hefei's internal and external defenses are now exceptionally solid.

Educational News

Important News: Shandong Province Increases Budget for Elementary and Secondary Schools 94

Jinan, 22nd: The Department of Education convened a budget meeting for provincial schools for the 21st year and decided to increase the number of high school classes by 28. According to statistics, there were 14,000 high school graduates in the province in the 20th year, and it is expected that 5,000 to 6,000 will go on to further education. Therefore, the number of provincial, county, and private junior high school classes will be increased by 33 to accommodate them. The provincial junior high school budget is 1,205,592 yuan, an increase of 77,198 yuan compared to the 20th year. The provincial elementary school budget is 192,420 yuan, an increase of 1,787 yuan compared to the 20th year.

Chen Jianxiao Takes Over as Director of Jiangxi Education Department 95

After the reorganization of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, former Director of Education Jiang Yi was hired by Chairman Xiong as a provincial government advisor, responsible for handling the affairs of the Department of Civil Affairs. Therefore, he repeatedly sent letters and telegrams urging the newly appointed Director of Education, Chen Jianxiao, to take office. Chen came to Jiangxi from Hankou to take the oath of office. In addition to retaining all the original staff, he also slightly changed the organization of the department. The original four sections of General Affairs, General, Specialized, and Social Affairs were changed to the first, second, third, and fourth sections. This was because the workload of the previous sections was uneven, and this change made things more balanced. Liu Fanguo, the former head of the General Affairs Section, who had been in charge for many years, was transferred to the position of secretary. Chen Yingkun, the former secretary during Chen Lijian's tenure as director, who is currently a secretary of the provincial government, was firmly requested to return to the department and continue to serve as secretary. There were not enough supervisors before, so two more were commissioned to conduct investigations of education in various counties and to supervise progress. The former Public Bulletin Editorial Office was transferred to the Jiangxi Compilation and Examination Office and became the editorial section, with its expenses being paid from the provincial education funds. Also, the address of the Education Department was originally borrowed from the former China-Thailand Bank's private housing. Now that it is being urgently requested back, the department moved to the former Shunzhi Guild Hall in front of the Dusi on the 13th and continues to work as usual.

Anhui Secondary School Society and Educational Association Established 96

Principals of provincial secondary schools and heads of social education institutions in Anhui took advantage of the opportunity to collect owed funds in Beijing and convened two meetings in a row. They collectively decided to establish a joint association of secondary schools and social education institutions. On January 16th, the charter was approved, and Wu Liangfu, Chen Dongyuan, Ke Defa, Zhang Su, and Wei Congxu were elected as standing committee members, and Cheng Mian and Gao Xifu were elected as alternate standing committee members.

Free Talk

Talks from the Not Removing Garden Grass Studio

One Lesson on Teaching a Son (Part 1) 110

In 1928, I bound a beautiful book with high-quality Xuan paper and placed it on my desk to prepare for students' questions and difficulties. A gold-painted label was pasted on the cover of this book, with the four characters "Life Problems" written by myself. Next to the book was a notice welcoming everyone to write out the questions in their hearts so that I could consider them in advance and then answer them. How poetic it is to write about things in your heart on a beautiful book! Needless to say, it is embarrassing to write chicken-foot characters on it. My purpose was achieved: before each student came to write a question, they had to practice some of the characters in the question many times before they were willing to write. Therefore, this book not only captured the steady stream of precious questions, but also unconsciously artisticized the characters used to write the questions. One day, I opened the book of life problems and found the following question:

"Can the master's teaching of his son be heard?"

The meaning of this question is extremely rich, giving a very profound stab. Since then, I have often asked myself: "How should this course of teaching a son be taught?" Now I publish the most recent lesson for the reference of people who have sons.

Strange Tales of a Doctor 111

— Yi Zang

In recent years, many students from our country have returned to the country with doctoral titles to show off. There are even those who have obtained two or three doctorates. The evening before yesterday, Ding Jun invited me to a banquet at Nanyuan Restaurant. Among the guests were Zhu, Zhang, and Liu, old friends. Zhu was also an American doctor of economics. During the drinking session, Zhang Jun talked about the Amomum villosum Doctor. Everyone thought the words were very bizarre and asked him why. Zhang Jun recounted the details, saying: Several years ago, there was a person named Jia who was fond of visiting prostitutes. His father was a prominent official. He stayed in Germany for ten years and never went to school to listen to lectures. He was demoted again and again. He lingered in dance halls and brothels and his classmates despised him. But he was shameless. He once said loudly: It is easy to get a doctorate. Why be diligent? People ridiculed him for being able to talk nonsense. Someone became angry and said: You are short-sighted and do not know the heroes. I will get one within a month. If I don't get it, I swear I will not return to China. After saying that, he flicked his sleeves and left. When he returned to his residence, he deeply regretted the rash words he had said that day. He hated his classmates for their ridicule and criticism. He was unhappy and paced around the room, thinking silently. He did not know what to do. Suddenly he remembered that there was a quack doctor in Chinatown. He sighed with inspiration: Alas, this can be done. He hurriedly visited the doctor and asked to borrow the Compendium of Materia Medica. He picked up a recipe and translated it into German. He called it the effect of Amomum villosum. He wrote a thesis on the Amomum villosum in the Compendium, distinguishing its warm and pungent properties, indications, and effects. He submitted it to the research institute. The scholars in the institute read it and thought it was strange. They praised it and gave him a doctorate in Amomum villosum. His name became famous. I do not dare to agree with Zhang Jun's words. In recent years, those who have obtained a doctorate in pharmacy with garlic and a doctorate in science with gold juice are almost all made in the same way as a certain doctor. Even the Japanese newspaper published this month revealed that a Chinese named Li obtained a doctorate in science by submitting a thesis on preserved duck eggs, which is enough to prove that the words are true.

World News in Brief 112

— Hai Ke

The speed of birds flying An American aviator. In order to know the speed of birds flying. Specially took a plane to chase the birds. The result obtained. Then I knew that geese can fly 52 to 56 miles per hour. Wild ducks can fly up to 46 miles per hour. Little grebes can fly 75 miles per hour. Burmese equality between men and women. Burmese equality between men and women. Can be regarded as the world's first. Even European and American countries that advocate equality between men and women. Also can't catch up. There is equality between their husband and wife. Regarding property. Whether it is a son or a daughter. All enjoy equal rights.

The Strong Enemy of the Perfume Industry Someone in Europe recently invented a chemical combination of perfume. Compared with perfumes made of flowers. The cost is less than one-tenth. The scent is strong. The well-known perfume companies in southern France. Will suffer a major blow.

Newly Invented Metal A large factory in the UK. A new metal was invented that is lighter than aluminum. Cheaper than copper. As solid as wrought iron. It can be bent after cooling. And impermeable to water. The country's navy has already adopted it.

Going to War 113

— A Member of the Youth Support the Military Corps

(10)(2) Arrives in Jinan

On New Year's Eve, we bid farewell to the old year in Xuzhou. It was the last moment within Jiangsu province. At this time, my heart was filled with both sorrow and joy. Sorrow for the daily decline of the nation's power, joy for the prospect of killing enemies. Finally, I recalled my kind parents, my loving sister, my lively younger brother, and my loyal nanny. But, after indulging in such reverie for nearly half an hour, in the end, the detestable nature of the brutal invaders inflamed my passion. Thus, all illusory thoughts vanished, reaffirming my fearless will.

On the afternoon of New Year's Day, we departed from Xuzhou and arrived in Jinan the next morning. Representatives from the provincial government were at the station to greet us, but we did not disembark because the commander told us, "It is said that there are spies of the Japanese bandits here, plotting against us." Before long, the municipal government bestowed upon us steamed buns and thin porridge, and other food items at the station. At that time, each of our stomachs was rumbling like thunder. Receiving this nourishment, we were all immensely grateful.

The mournful cries of crows were carried by the wind into the carriages. The vast twilight gradually enveloped everything outside the window. Everything faded away, but I could see the lights illuminating the silver-clad roadside, incessantly exuding a biting cold. Many comrades were asleep, but I was still wandering alone. Suddenly, I heard a burst of loud noise. I couldn't help but jump off the platform, left the station, and ran straight into the city streets. I suddenly saw thousands of Japanese beasts rampaging wildly. Flesh torn by bullets flew everywhere. Anyone hit would fall, and any building hit would burst into flames. I was about to turn back to report to the commander when I suddenly heard cries for help from a side street. I followed the cries to the inner room of a shop. Alas, a female compatriot was lying there, her lower body naked, like a dying white dove frantically flapping its wings because it couldn't breathe, struggling with a ferocious bandit. Beside the bed, a young man lay on the ground, covered in blood. My anger flared up, and I shouted, "You beasts, cease your impudence!" Before I could finish speaking, I was grabbed from behind, and both my hands were bound with rope. I turned my head to look inside and recognized another soldier beast. He grabbed me and dragged me out the door, and I vaguely arrived at a place. At the door, a sign seemed to read "Jinan..." This beast soldier led me inside and tied me to a pillar. I saw layers upon layers of beastly shadows surrounding a compatriot tied to another pillar, shouting incomprehensibly for a while. Finally, one by one, they each punched that compatriot and left. After a while, several burly brutes with faces full of fat came in. They saw that the compatriot had black eyes and swollen ears, a weak body, and a faint breath, but they grinned sinisterly. One of them drew a bayonet from his waist. In a flash, blood gushed forth, and the compatriot's nose was sliced off. I was furious and strained against my bonds, but then I heard someone ask, "What's going on? What's going on?" I turned my gaze towards the four walls and realized that I was in a carriage. Only then did I understand that the humiliation of the May 3rd Massacre was like this...

Images from a Northern Tour and Other Things (4) 114

— Yao Su Feng

An Autobiography by Movie Star Hu Die

For the past few years, my satisfaction has depended on the praise of many dear audience members, and my position has also made good progress; however, I myself have only ever obtained satisfaction once. My photos being plastered all over newspapers is not what satisfies me; my name, larger than a bowl, in advertisements is not what satisfies me; all the mementos that reward me and praise me are not what satisfies me. So, what exactly satisfies me? And why have I only been satisfied once? When I talk about it, I don’t know who to thank. It turns out that in the early summer of the twentieth year of the Republic [1931], the Star Film Company suddenly received many letters from strangers. All of these letters were addressed to Mr. Zhang Shichuan and Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu; the addresses of the senders, some were from Shanghai, some from the Northeast, some from Beiping, some from Southeast Asia; although the sentences in the letters were different, they had the same meaning. Until the end of July, within twenty or thirty days, a total of more than one hundred and seventy letters were received, all saying, "Why doesn't your company film [Tixiao Yinyuan] Fate in Tears and Laughter?... With Hu Die playing He Lina and Fengxi..." Ah! How surprising and ashamed it makes one feel! At least, I had more than one hundred and seventy sympathizers. This was the only time since I appeared on the screen that I have felt genuinely satisfied.

Afterwards, after the plan to shoot Fate in Tears and Laughter was confirmed, we began preparations to start work. I also took the time to read through Fate in Tears and Laughter. Although I felt that Fengxi, in the book of that era, was not a person I could portray, the fact was that I had to work hard to take on this heavy task. I remember that at that time, "Sing-song Girl Red Peony," in which I starred, was being shown at the New Light Grand Theatre and was sold out for seven days, so naturally I was very happy; many people said that it was my most satisfactory work, and even many people said that I should change my previous style and become a performer of tears like Pearly Lin Gan-xu. However, for the sake of Fate in Tears and Laughter, I didn't quite believe this opinion. I seemed to be somewhat overconfident; I might even be overconfident. I will wait until Fate in Tears and Laughter is successful, and let the dear audience give me an honest critique!

New Words on Planting Rice Seedlings 115

— Bu Jiasheng

I have often said that the more prosperous the surface of Shanghai becomes, the darker its underside becomes. Their progress proceeds at the same speed. Swindling is one aspect of the dark side of Shanghai. The techniques employed are constantly evolving, making it impossible for people to guard against them. Therefore, I will describe a recent event to inform the readers. There is a Huada Pharmacy on Foch Road, which mainly deals in "Lion Brand" beef and chicken broth products from the German Malta Pharmaceutical Factory. In recent years, sales have continued to grow, extending to Southeast Asia. Some people come to Shanghai with cash to purchase wholesale. On the morning of the fourth day, someone claiming to be Hu Fuqing, a representative from the Zhuyu Long Firm in Lanxi, came to the pharmacy to purchase sixty cases of beef broth and one case of chicken broth, with a total value of over nine hundred yuan. Hu presented a note for one thousand taels issued by Henglong and payable at the Ankang Money Exchange in Shanghai on the eighth day. The pharmacy then agreed with Hu that they would cash the note on the eighth day and pick up the goods on the tenth day. One thousand taels converted to over one thousand three hundred yuan. After deducting the price of the goods, there was still a surplus of more than four hundred yuan. The pharmacy issued a check from the Jiangsu Bank for the remaining amount, dated the twelfth, believing that since there was no cash payment, there was no need to worry. Moreover, the pharmacy has always had a 0.99 commission for wholesale, as a reward for the intermediary. The goods purchased by Hu were actually worth over nine hundred yuan, and a commission of nine yuan and some cents should be given. Since it was already paid at that time, this commission should be paid. The pharmacy did not want to give the commission in cash, since Hu did not purchase with cash, preferring to lose a few more cents. They also issued a check for ten yuan dated the twelfth. With such caution, the swindlers would have no way to use their tricks. Unexpectedly, after Hu took the check, he actually changed the date from the twelfth to the fourth and went to the Jiangsu Bank to cash it. The Jiangsu Bank did not notice and actually paid out over four hundred yuan. When it was discovered, the so-called Hu Fuqing had disappeared without a trace. The pharmacy tentatively took the note to Ankang to cash it, but they said that the original note had not arrived. It was not until the eleventh day that they despondently stopped going to cash it.

The Tale of the Two Soldiers (18) 116

— Master of the Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter Three: Two Talents Arrive Together, Scattering the Banquet; Yin and Xing Avoid Each Other, Who Left the Jewel Box?

Here was Liang Xiaoyun, as beautiful as a flower, in my own room, drinking and chatting intimately. If she were to run over and catch us in the act, women's minds are narrow and their jealousy is strong. It would inevitably make these two radiant rivals feel like they had splinters in their eyes at the same time, causing great unhappiness. And the one caught in the middle, facing difficulties on both sides, would only be me. Although Liang Xiaoyun might not say anything, Li Wenxia has a tongue like a sharp sword and a mouth like a torrent, never willing to easily forgive others. Moreover, if she were to catch her with some faults, she would certainly launch a major campaign of accusation afterward, bringing out some great principles of ancient sages and worthies, speaking eloquently and reproaching me for inviting idlers and strangers into the house to drink and make merry behind her back when I had suffered such a great tragedy, putting my parents' grievances and the mourning in my funeral attire completely out of my mind, forgetting them completely. She would ask where my heart was and where my sense of righteousness lay. At that time, she would be righteous and have plenty to say, but how would I face her and what words would I use to answer? Bad, bad, bad. I can't just wait for her to come and catch my mistake and cause so much trouble. While there is still time, I should quickly run back to the room and make an excuse to get Liang Xiaoyun to leave first, so that the two of them will forever be a pair of Yin and Xing avoiding each other, in order to avoid some unnecessary arguments and maintain world peace. Thinking that time was of the essence, I immediately ran back to the room in a panic. Seeing Liang Xiaoyun sitting upright on the edge of the seat, waiting for me, I was about to ask her to leave as soon as I opened my mouth, but I don't know why I was a little cowardly at the last minute. For a moment, I hesitated and couldn't say anything, and instead, my face turned purple and I gasped for breath, and I still obediently sat down with her. Liang Xiaoyun had been sitting here alone for a long time, and she was already feeling lonely and anxious. She was secretly wondering which important friend was calling, causing him to rush around and leave her alone in the cold, without even showing a little courtesy. When he ran back, she took a closer look at him and found that he was distracted and his face was haggard, even more agitated than before. She couldn't help but be very surprised and couldn't help but ask, "What's wrong with you? I just heard someone call and you rushed off like that. When you came back, your face looked even worse. Who was this call from? What did they say? Could it be that there is some new information from your family?" An Yutian was worried about how to lie, but her words happened to open up a path for him. He answered her, "That's right. Another person has come from my hometown. They will be coming here in a while. However, this person is a senior elder. If you are here, it might not be convenient to meet them. So I want to discuss with you and ask you to leave first. Tomorrow I will definitely go to your place and have a long chat."

A Disastrous Drop of 15 Taels and 8 Mace

Yesterday, the gold standard money market experienced even more severe declines, with deteriorating conditions. There was only limited recovery, and the atmosphere was filled with panic and fear. Although there was no specific news from abroad, it was actually caused by large investors selling off in droves. Foreign Interest Rates Exceeded 2% 120

Due to Strong Buying Interest

Interbank Lending Rates Also High at 6%

Market Overview. Yesterday's financial market, from a superficial observation, did not have any major news. However, the sudden increase in foreign interest rates, which exceeded 7 qian and 2 fen yesterday afternoon, was noteworthy in the market. Although the current increase in interest rates was unexpected, it was a precedent for the year-end accounting period. In previous years, there were too many repayments at this time, so prices had to fall.

Interest Rate Prices. The buying interest in "foreign interest" was too strong in the morning, and the supply side became hesitant, so the interest rate rose, increasing by 0.5% compared to the high price of the previous afternoon, to 7 qian, 1.0825 fen. Unexpectedly, in the afternoon market, the early market was unable to buy enough, so prices had to be raised to purchase, resulting in a surge of more than 2%, exceeding 2%, to 7 qian, 2.05%. As a result, the price increased by a total of 3.025% compared to the early market of the previous day. The "silver interest" rate was 1.4% in both the morning and afternoon markets, an increase of 6% compared to the previous day. Banks listed rates at 6% plus 4-5%.

Subsidiary Coin Market. The price of Jiangnan small silver was slightly lower due to scarce transactions. Discussion of Interest Rates During the Year-End Accounting Period 121

As a rule, every year-end accounting period, in order to facilitate the closing of accounts, there is a custom of deciding on the interest rate settlement in advance. Yesterday, the Money Trade Association decided that the interest rate for savings from January 1st to January 20th would be calculated at 3.95%, and the interest rate for savings from January 21st to January 31st would be calculated at 2.95%. Interest on arrears would still be added at the sitting rate of 4.5%.

Local News

Municipal Government Lodges Protest Against Japanese Riot Case 137

Secretary-General Yu Announces the Course of Sino-Japanese Negotiations

Regarding the Incident of Japanese Rioters Burning Down the Sanyou Industrial Company Factory

Yesterday, the Municipal Government filed a serious written protest with the Japanese Consulate, and Secretary-General Yu also made an important statement regarding this case. A summary is as follows:

Secretary-General Yu's Statement: Yesterday, reporters visited Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun and inquired about the recent Sino-Japanese negotiations in the city. He replied as follows: On the 18th of this month, at around 5 o'clock, the Municipal Government received a report that five Japanese monks were beaten by rioters in Yinxiang Township. It immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau to investigate the truth as soon as possible. According to a report from the Public Security Bureau to the Municipal Government, five Japanese monks, including Tenzaki Keisho, Mizukami Hideyu, and Buddhist followers Goto Yoshihei, Kurodani Asatsujiro, and Fujimura Kuniyoshi, held a winter practice religious ceremony on the 10th. While passing behind the Sanyou Towel Factory on Mayushan Road, they were attacked by rioters. Tenzaki, Mizukami, and Goto were slower to escape and were seriously injured, lying on the roadside. They were later sent to the Sacred Heart Hospital on Ningguo Road in the Public Concession for treatment by the Fifth District Fourth Office. The remaining Kurodani and Fujimura suffered lighter injuries and reported to the Yangshupu Police Station themselves. They were sent to the hospital by the police car. As for the rioters, they could not be arrested on the spot because the area was remote and there were no posts. The Municipal Government immediately ordered the bureau to arrest the perpetrators within a time limit and bring them to justice. On the morning of the 19th, Japanese Consul-General Murai Kuramatsu visited the Mayor. The Mayor had not yet returned to Shanghai, so he was received by me. The Japanese Consul immediately made an oral protest regarding the case. I informed him that the details of the case were being investigated, but since it had been reported that Japanese people were injured by Chinese people on Chinese territory, it was unfortunate and should be regretted. That afternoon, I visited the Japanese Consul and requested that he restrain the overseas Chinese and wait quietly for a resolution. Unexpectedly, the next day (the 20th), I received a report that the Japanese had set fire to the Sanyou Towel Factory of a Chinese merchant in the early morning and killed a Chinese policeman on duty in the Public Concession and injured two Chinese policemen. I believed that this kind of violent and illegal act by the Japanese was inexcusable and immediately visited the Japanese Consul that day to make an oral protest. The Japanese Consul expressed regret and stated that he would be responsible for arresting the perpetrators and handling the matter seriously. The day before yesterday (the 21st) morning, when the Japanese Consul visited the Mayor at the Municipal Government, he personally expressed his regret to the Mayor and presented a written protest regarding the case of the injured Japanese monks, making four requests: (1) The Mayor must express his apology to the Consul-General; (2) The search, arrest, and punishment of the perpetrators should be carried out quickly and effectively; (3) Medical expenses and compensation should be given to the five victims; (4) Illegal and outrageous actions such as anti-Japanese and insulting Japan should be strictly prohibited, and the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Committee and various anti-Japanese groups should be dissolved immediately. Mayor Wu immediately gave an oral reply, stating that regarding the third item, Chinese law had explicit provisions for the punishment of injury crimes, and the perpetrators would be arrested and dealt with according to law. As for items one and three, they could also be considered. However, the fourth item concerned the people's movement, and if it was within the scope of the law, he had no right to prohibit it. If there were illegal actions, they would be punished according to law. Mayor Wu had gone to Beijing that evening to ask for instructions. As for the case of the Japanese setting fire to the Sanyou Towel Factory of a Chinese merchant and killing and injuring Chinese policemen, the Municipal Government issued a written protest to the Japanese Consul yesterday. This is the course of the Municipal Government's handling of the recent Sino-Japanese negotiations in the city. The Municipal Government's handling of all cases, whether they are domestic or foreign, will be handled fairly and according to law. For example, regarding the case of obstructing the Japanese monks, the Japanese monks were innocently beaten, and the perpetrators will be strictly arrested and brought to justice. As for the actions of the Japanese forming a team to burn Chinese factories and kill and injure Chinese policemen on duty, serious negotiations should be carried out to achieve the desired goals. At the same time, the local area should be strictly guarded to ensure the safety of the urban area.

Serious Protest by the Municipal Government: At 3:00 PM yesterday, the Municipal Government specifically filed a serious protest with the Japanese Consulate regarding the arson case at the Sanyou Factory. The text reads, "Dear Sir, according to a report from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, at 2:20 AM on the 20th of this month, dozens of young Japanese people sneaked outside the Sanyou Cotton Weaving Factory on Mayushan Road in Yinxiang Port in this city and set fire to four places. At that time, the workers were asleep due to the late hour and did not notice. Later, the factory staff carefully investigated and according to nearby villagers, the Japanese used fire wine, gasoline, sulfur, and other substances to guide the arson. At that time, there were three Chinese policemen on duty at the nearby police booth. Upon hearing the alarm, they immediately called the fire brigade for help. The Japanese surrounded the booth and used knives to injure Chinese policeman No. 3029. Chinese policeman No. 1116 was stabbed and fell to the ground. The telephone was cut and thrown into the nearby river. Another Chinese policeman No. 765 was chased to Linqing Road by the Japanese and killed with sharp blades. The Japanese then fled without a trace. The factory was burned and suffered great losses." Based on this, it was found that the Japanese dared to form a team in the early morning to set fire to and destroy a domestic factory and kill Chinese policemen on duty. Not only is it not tolerated by the law, but at this time of many events, the impact is particularly serious. In addition to immediately sending personnel to file a protest, the following conditions are specifically proposed: (1) The Japanese Consul-General expresses his apology to the Mayor; (2) The arsonists and murderers are quickly arrested and severely punished; (3) Full compensation is paid to the victims, and the amount of compensation is negotiated separately; (4) A firm guarantee is made that similar incidents will not occur in the future. The Mayor sincerely hopes that your Consul will sincerely fulfill the above articles so that this case can be resolved quickly, disputes can be resolved, and friendly relations between the two countries can be maintained. A letter is sent accordingly, please investigate. To Murai Kuramatsu, Consul-General of Japan stationed in Shanghai, Mayor Wu Techeng.

Japanese Memorandum Says 138

The City Government Denies Receipt

Japanese Residents' General Meeting Today

Chinese Authorities on Alert

Since the Japanese residents' riot occurred, the situation in this port has reached a critical point. The Japanese side insists that after the Japanese Consul-General Murai submitted a request to Mayor Wu, demanding the immediate dissolution of anti-Japanese groups, the Japanese Navy Commander Shiozawa also submitted an ultimatum to the city government the night before last, preparing to use force as a backing. It is further said that this final warning was also sent to the Public Works Department for reference. The Japanese newspapers have stated this with certainty, and the local English-language "North China Daily News" also recorded this matter. However, neither the city government nor the Public Works Department had received the memorandum as of last night. Last night, our newspaper reporter further inquired about the truth from the Japanese side. It was claimed that what the Japanese Navy Commander had submitted was not an ultimatum, but a statement containing the nature of a final warning. It was also said that the Japanese Navy and consulate authorities have a firm attitude. If Mayor Wu does not give a satisfactory reply to their demands, they will resolutely use force against certain organizations. The Japanese who died in the fight with the Chinese police in the International Settlement at Yinxiang Port are scheduled to be buried today, and the Japanese residents will then hold a general meeting. It is feared that incidents may occur. The Public Works Department stated that they would maintain the peace in the International Settlement, but will act as they see fit.

Foreign Press Reports: According to the "North China Daily News," on Thursday evening,

Rear Admiral Shiozawa, Commander of the Japanese Fleet stationed in China, sent an ultimatum to the Mayor of Shanghai, demanding a satisfactory response to the Japanese Consul-General's protest against the anti-Japanese movement and the assault on Japanese residents, and demanding the dissolution of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association and other anti-Japanese groups. If these demands are not met, the Japanese naval authorities will take appropriate measures to protect the rights and interests of Japanese people. Commander Shiozawa also sent copies of this ultimatum to the Japanese Consulate, the Public Works Department, and the Public Security Bureau.

Advertisement in Japanese Newspaper: Yesterday, the Headquarters of the First Japanese Fleet stationed in Shanghai published an advertisement in a local Japanese newspaper, stating that if the city government's reply is not satisfactory, the fleet will take stern countermeasures.

Yu Hongjun Speaks: Yesterday, a reporter from the "Japan-China News Agency" asked Secretary Yu Hongjun of the city government whether the Japanese fleet commander had submitted an ultimatum. Mr. Yu strongly denied it, saying that since the Japanese atrocities occurred, apart from a protest letter from the Japanese Consul regarding the assault on a monk, the city government had not received a single document from the Japanese side. The reports in the British and American newspapers that the ultimatum was submitted by the commander of the Japanese fleet stationed in Shanghai are untrue. The commander of the Japanese fleet stationed in Shanghai has no right to make any written or oral demands directly to this government. Such rumors are simply absurd.

Japanese Residents' General Meeting: Japanese residents of this city will hold a general meeting at the Peng Road Club at 3:00 PM today. According to inquiries, after the Japanese finish their meeting, they will organize a procession to North Sichuan Road and other places in Hongkou.

Authorities on Alert: The city government yesterday specifically ordered the Public Security Bureau to take appropriate precautions. After receiving the order, the Municipal Public Security Bureau ordered the Sixth Squadron Leader Sun Mou of the Police Brigade to lead more than 130 policemen from his entire squadron to be stationed near the border between the Chinese and International Settlements in North Sichuan Road, and to jointly defend with the police from various districts of the Fifth District. If necessary, the troops from the joint defense office of the army and police of the Zhabei Huzhou Guild Hall can assist nearby. The precautions were already very thorough last night. The authorities of the International Settlement, also for the sake of maintaining public order, have prepared several police vehicles and reserve forces of the Volunteer Corps and Chinese and Western detectives to patrol the Hongkou area closely.

Hoping for 10 Million Yuan Per Month

Representatives from all circles in Shanghai, including Li Fuxun, Zhang Gongquan, Qin Runqing, Wang Xiaolai, Shi Liangcai, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, etc., previously discussed with Mayor Wu Tiecheng on assisting the central government in its financial difficulties and drafted five principles. Yesterday, President Sun Ke of the Executive Yuan sent a telegram to the six major organizations in this port, providing answers regarding the content of the principles and requesting monthly assistance of ten million yuan to stabilize the overall situation. The original telegram is as follows: Shanghai Jianghai Customs 2.5% Surtax National Treasury Bond Fund Custody Committee, National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Shanghai Banking Association of Shanghai, Shanghai Money Trade Association, and the Holders Association of Domestic Public Bonds and Treasury Bills of the Republic of China, all respectfully informed. Minister Huang Hanliang of the Ministry of Finance forwarded the telegram from Vice Minister Lin Kanghou, which has been carefully read. The government deeply sympathizes with the consolidation of credit. The Ministry of Finance has been ordered to instruct the Customs and Salt Administration and the Inspectorate General of Customs to handle the matter diligently. The tax supervision provision can be temporarily retained. As for the Central Bank, in accordance with the resolutions of the Peace Conference, it is now separated from politics. The Minister of Finance no longer concurrently serves as the Governor, which is already a fact. Furthermore, Vice Governor Xu is publicly recommended by the financial community, so there are no problems. However, military and political expenses have been repeatedly reduced, and the needs are still great. It is hoped that the people will cooperate with the government and strive to provide ten million yuan per month to stabilize the overall situation. This is earnestly hoped for. Special telegram reply from Sun Ke, President of the Executive Yuan. Ma.

Huang Hanliang Arrives in Shanghai 140

Negotiating Loans with the Shanghai Financial Community Yesterday

Vice Minister Lin Kanghou Also Officially Assumed Office Yesterday

The Financial Community Has Agreed to a Loan of Eight Million

Complete Negotiations Should Be Completed Within Two or Three Days

Huang Hanliang, the Acting Minister of Finance, resigned in anger previously because someone in the central government proposed a plan to suspend the payment of principal and interest on bonds, and he was unable to prevent it. Vice Minister Lin Kanghou also continued to submit his resignation. Now, the central government's plan to suspend the payment of principal and interest has been canceled, and both Huang and Lin have been strongly urged to remain in their positions by the Executive Yuan. Huang officially assumed his duties in the ministry the day before yesterday and came to Shanghai from Beijing the night before last to negotiate financial issues. He arrived at the Finance Office on the Bund at 10:00 AM yesterday morning and immediately convened the Shanghai banking community to discuss loans. The details are summarized as follows:

Morning Talks: After arriving at the office, Huang and Lin immediately convened the heads of the Shanghai banking community for talks, stating that the central government's military and political expenses were urgently needed and should be discussed immediately. Those who attended included Zhang Gongquan, Li Fuxun, Bei Songsun, Chen Guangfu,

Xu Jiyin, and others. Huang stated at the time that the central financial

situation was difficult and that he had repeatedly sought loans from the Shanghai banking community. He said that the Shanghai community deeply understood the central government's financial difficulties and agreed to maintain it, but the amount had not yet been agreed upon. He said that he had reassumed his position as Minister of Finance and that the current difficulty was this matter. He sincerely asked the Shanghai community to do everything possible to maintain national finances. Everyone present expressed their agreement and promised to do their best to mediate with the Shanghai community.

Afternoon Meeting: At 6:00 PM in the afternoon, Huang and Lin reconvened the entire Shanghai banking community, money trade, and exchange representatives. The bank representatives included Bei Songsun from the Bank of China, Hu Mengjia from the Bank of Communications, Xu Xinliu from the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Chen Guangfu from the Shanghai Bank, Chen Zheqing from the Salt Bank, Sun Jingxi from the Zhongfu Bank, Yu Huikui from the Juxingcheng Bank, Sun Hengfu from the Siming Bank, Yao Desheng from the China Bank, Wu Yunzhai from the Jin Cheng Bank, Wang Zhixin from the Xinhua Bank, Wu Weiru from the Donghua Bank, Ye Fuxiao from the Dalu Bank, Xu Baoqi from the Yongheng Bank, Liu Huizhi from the China Industrial Bank, Wang Xinguan from the Commercial Bank of China, Hu Bijiang from the Zhongnan Bank, Xu Yeming from the Hefeng Bank, Xu Youming from the Jiangsu Bank, Tang Shoumin from the Guohua Bank, Wang Boyuan from the Kenye Bank, Zhang Rongfu from the Guangdong Bank, Ling Wenli from the Dongya Bank, Wang Tianjia from the Zhongxing Bank, and Qi Yunqing from the Agricultural and Industrial Bank. Representatives from the money trade included Pei Yunqing, and representatives from the exchange included Zhang Weiru, among others. Huang presided over the meeting, reporting on the circumstances of his reinstatement and the urgent need for the central government's finances to be maintained by all sectors. The representatives spoke one after another, expressing their willingness to do their best to maintain the loan issue, but requested that the central government be aware of the difficulties of the current situation and find ways to further reduce expenses. The meeting adjourned at around 8:00 PM.

Loan Amount: According to a certain representative of the banking community who attended yesterday's meeting, speaking to a reporter from the "East China News Agency," Huang's visit to Shanghai to raise loans was a continuation of the scope of discussions that Wu Tiecheng had with various Shanghai organizations some time ago. The central government still needs a large sum of ten million yuan. The Shanghai community still hopes to strive to reduce it, but according to the results of yesterday's discussion, the Shanghai organizations have agreed to try to raise eight million yuan. Huang is also willing to report to the central government. This loan will be jointly borne by the banking and money trade sectors and the exchange. It should be completed within three to five days, but how the banking, money trade, and exchange sectors will allocate the burden has not yet been agreed upon.

Huang's Statement: A reporter from the "East China News Agency" visited Huang yesterday, asking the following questions: (1) After canceling his resignation this time, what new plans does he have for the future of finance? (2) Has the interception of taxes by various provinces been completely eliminated? (3) Has the Shanghai banking industry agreed to a loan of eight million yuan? (4) How to maintain the sharp decline in public bonds? Huang asked Vice Minister Lin Kanghou to answer on his behalf: (1) After canceling his resignation this time, there are plans to reorganize and maintain financial issues, which will be implemented successively. (2) The central government has issued a unified order to all provinces not to intercept taxes, and most provinces have expressed that they will not intercept taxes. (3) The loan amount from the Shanghai banking community, eight million yuan, is getting closer, but is still under negotiation. (4) There is a complete plan to maintain public bonds, and the Customs Service has been ordered to prepare a security form for the public bond fund to ensure that the people of the country are convinced of the reliability of public bonds.

Lin's Statement: Lin then stated to a reporter from the "East China News Agency" that he had reassumed his position as Vice Minister of Finance, but only to assist in everything as a representative of the people, so that the central government's finances could safely pass the Lunar New Year. He said that he would only serve until the Lunar New Year. He added that if the provinces did not intercept tax revenues, it would be possible to reorganize China's finances.

Customs Revenue and Expenditure for the Year 1931 141

Customs revenue for the year 1931 (import tax, export tax, transit tax, and tonnage dues), calculated in round numbers, totaled 24,606,400 taels of Haikwan silver. This includes (1) 12,821,300 taels of Haikwan silver, which is the amount converted from 10,916,100 gold units collected according to the gold unit tariff; (2) 7,374,900 taels of Haikwan silver, which is the amount of Haikwan silver actually received according to the gold unit tariff, based on the prevailing gold and silver prices; (3) 4,410,200 taels of Haikwan silver, which is the amount of tax collected according to the Haikwan silver tariff, the actual amount of Haikwan silver received. The total of these three items is 24,606,400 taels of Haikwan silver.

The total customs revenue for the year 1931 is 24,831,400 taels of Haikwan silver. The disaster relief surtax collected on imports and exports in December 1931 totaled 1,025,000 taels of Haikwan silver (calculated in round numbers).

The total is 119,813,009.08 Customs Taels. Compared to the amount paid in 1930 (91,474,349.31 Customs Taels), this year's actual expenditure is 28,338,659.77 Customs Taels more. Naval Ship "Yuzhang" Sinks in Nantong 143

All Officers and Crew Rescued

Navy Department Decides to Salvage

The Jiangyuan warship of the Second Fleet of the Navy unfortunately ran aground and sank near Xinghua Port in Fujian last year. The Mitsubishi Salvage Company managed to salvage it, tow it to Shanghai, and put it in dry dock for repairs. It took four months and cost more than 100,000 yuan to complete the repairs. It had just been completed the day before yesterday and was heading to Beijing to participate in the exercises. Unexpectedly, the Yuzhang torpedo boat of the torpedo boat fleet ran aground and sank in Lujing Port, Nantong Prefecture, at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday. The details are as follows:

Circumstances of the Sinking: The ship was originally stationed in Nantong. At 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, it received an order from the Navy Department to go to Zhenjiang. Unexpectedly, when approaching Lujing Port, it suddenly encountered dense fog and lost its way, running aground on the Qingtian Reef. At that time, the tide was surging and there was no way to rescue it, so it sank.

Crew Rescued: At that time, the Daqing ship of the Dada Company happened to pass by, so it managed to rescue all the officers and crew of the ship to the ship. At the same time, the Yingrui warship, which was stationed in Jiangyin, was the first to receive a radio report from the Daqing ship about the accident and sailed to the scene. At around 7:00 PM, it approached the Daqing ship and transferred the Yuzhang crew from the Daqing to the Yingrui. The headquarters of the First Fleet of the Navy in this port received a radio report from the Yingrui at around 8:00 PM the night before last, reporting the details of the accident.

Salvage Operations Underway: At around 10:00 AM yesterday morning, Li Shijia, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Navy Department and Acting Permanent Vice Minister, went to the headquarters of the First Fleet to discuss the aftermath with Vice Minister Chen Jiliang. However, the exact circumstances of the accident and the current state of the ship are not yet known, so it is difficult to determine the responsibility of the personnel in charge of the ship. However, salvage operations have already been actively launched.

Total Number of Crew Members: The ship had a total of 81 officers and crew members, including one captain with the rank of colonel, one executive officer with the rank of lieutenant commander, one chief engineer with the rank of lieutenant commander, one torpedo and electrical officer with the rank of lieutenant, one assistant engineer with the rank of lieutenant, one assistant electrical officer with the rank of lieutenant junior grade, one navigator with the rank of lieutenant, one clerk with the rank of second lieutenant, one assistant electrical officer with the rank of second lieutenant, two warrant officer chief engineers, one warrant officer chief gunner, one warrant officer chief engineer, one warrant officer chief torpedo officer, one warrant officer chief electrician, and 66 sailors. All were rescued.

Ship's Overview: The ship was built in Germany in the second year of the Xuantong reign (1910). There were a total of three ships, including the Jiankang and Jianwei in addition to the Yuzhang. The price was more than 1.4 million taels. The displacement was 390 tons, the length was 208 feet, the width was 21 feet, and the depth was 10 feet. The armament included two 2-inch guns, four 2-pound guns, and eighteen 2-inch torpedoes. During the exercises in Xiangshan Port last year, it lost a torpedo in the sea. It took a week to recover it. The captain, Ren Guanghai, is on sick leave, and all ship affairs are currently being handled by the executive officer, Feng, on an acting basis.

Japanese Warships Arrive in Shanghai Today 145

Six Warships and a Squadron of Aircraft

500 Marines Land

The Japanese Navy Ministry is dispatching a large naval force to Shanghai, which is expected to arrive today. The information obtained yesterday is as follows:

Destroyers Arriving: The warships dispatched to Shanghai by the Japanese Navy Ministry this time, which are being dispatched from the Wu naval port, are the cruiser Oi and the second-class destroyers Fuji, Kuzu, Usu, and Hagi. The Oi cruiser has a displacement of 5,100 tons and has eight 14 cm guns and two 14 cm anti-aircraft guns. The four destroyers have a displacement of 770 tons each, a speed of 33 knots, and each has three 12 cm guns, three 8 cm guns, and four torpedo tubes. They have already set sail. As of last night, they have not yet been seen. According to the Japanese side, they should enter the Huangpu River by this morning at the latest and will be stationed in the Yangshupu area. Aircraft Carrier to Follow: In addition to the five ships, the aircraft carrier Notoro, carrying several aircraft, has also been dispatched to Shanghai. The aircraft carrier has a displacement of 10,000 tons and is equipped with two 14 cm guns and four 8 cm anti-aircraft guns. It is following the Oi and other ships to Shanghai. It is expected to arrive in the Huangpu River this afternoon.

Marines Dispatched to Shanghai: There are already 500 Japanese marines in Shanghai. This time, 500 special marines are being dispatched from the naval corps of the Wu Zhen garrison, arriving in Shanghai on the Oi cruiser. It is planned that they will land at the Huishan Wharf after entering the port today. The Japanese naval commander in Shanghai has already arranged the location for their stationing.

Japanese Marines Demand Correction from "Min Kuo Daily News" Yesterday 146

According to the Central News Agency, at 5:00 PM yesterday, Lieutenant Tomiyama Hiroshi of the Japanese Marine Corps headquarters brought a letter to the "Min Kuo Daily News" and visited the newspaper's authorities, claiming that the "Min Kuo Daily News" report on the incident in which the Sanyou Factory in Yinxiang Port was burned down by Japanese ruffians on the 20th of this month, stated that the marine corps had provided cover, which was inconsistent with the facts. Four demands were made. The newspaper's authorities replied that the news was published based on reports from various sources. Since it was stated that it was inconsistent with the facts, it should be corrected immediately. The original letter from the Japanese Marine Corps headquarters to the "Min Kuo Daily News" is as follows: To the editor of the "Min Kuo Daily News," the article "Japanese Ruffians Protected by Marines" published in the second edition of your newspaper on the 21st of this month is completely contrary to the facts and deliberately damages the reputation of this marine corps. We hereby solemnly demand the following four items from your editor: (1) The editor must come to the team to submit a written apology. (2) Publish a letter of apology covering half a page. (3) Guarantee that such incidents will not happen again in the future. (4) Dismiss the directly responsible reporter. A reply is required by 5:00 AM tomorrow (23rd). If you do not comply, do not blame us. Japanese Marine Corps, 5:00 PM, January 22, Showa 7 (1932).

Note from the Central News Agency: The misspellings and ungrammatical passages in the letter are all in the original text.

News Roundup of the Two Anti-Japanese Organizations 147

Emergency Meeting of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association: The Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association convened an emergency meeting of its executive committee yesterday in response to the riots in Shanghai by the Japanese. Chu Huiseng was elected chairman. The chairman began by reporting the purpose of the meeting. After passionate speeches by various committee members, the following resolutions were passed: (1) issue a declaration; (2) telegraph the central government to sever diplomatic relations with Japan; (3) request the municipal government to reject all unreasonable demands from the Japanese side; (4) notify all sectors to adopt appropriate self-defense measures; (5) appoint Zhu Zifan and Gong Yuting as representatives of the association to express sympathy to the workers of the Sanyou Industrial Company and the citizens of Yinxiang Port. (1) Declaration: The violent Japanese, relying on their military force, have invaded and occupied the territory of our three northeastern provinces and slaughtered countless of our compatriots. All Chinese people are filled with grief and indignation. Even before the bloodstains of Shenyang are dry, the disturbances in Tianjin and Qingdao have risen again. After the party headquarters in Qingdao was burned, the tragedy in Fujian revived. With such violent acts violating international conventions and disrupting world peace, the Japanese have not repented. Now, they dare to carry out their murderous and arsonist behavior in Shanghai, the economic center of the world. This is not only a loss of international courtesy to the people of the Republic of China, but also a fundamental shaking of the security of the Shanghai Public Concession. If this can be tolerated, what cannot be tolerated? Our association, born from all sectors of Shanghai, bears the important mission of resisting Japan and saving the nation. At this critical juncture, we must intensify our work and never succumb to the threats and coercion of the violent Japanese. We dare to solemnly declare that we hope that the citizens of Shanghai will face the crisis of national destruction and family ruin with a determination to break the cauldrons and sink the boats. On the one hand, they should seek appropriate self-defense, and on the other hand, they should thoroughly implement economic severance. Our colleagues in the association will be committed to this cause from beginning to end, even unto death. We respectfully submit this declaration for your public consideration. (2) Telegram to the National Government: To Chairman Lin of the Nanjing National Government and Minister Chen of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: The violent Japanese, relying on their military force, have invaded our territory, harmed our people, disregarded international law, and disrupted world peace. For several months, such brutal acts have been numerous. Even before the bloodstains of Shenyang are dry, the tragedy in Tianjin has followed. We are struggling to resist Japan and save the nation, but the Japanese are intensifying their actions, daring to openly expose their ferocious faces in Shanghai, the center of culture and commerce, committing murder and arson, recklessly disregarding everything, and deploying troops and generals as if facing a major enemy. Such barbarism is not self-aware and has even made unreasonable demands on our country’s authorities. If this can be tolerated, what cannot be tolerated? Our colleagues in the association believe that this kind of action by the violent Japanese is clearly a planned and organized step, not an accidental outbreak. This proves that the violent Japanese have no respect for international etiquette towards our country. We urge the government to make a decisive decision and declare a severance of diplomatic relations with Japan. If we continue to compromise, we fear the country will perish soon. Our colleagues in the association have the determination to resist Japan and save the nation. Even if we are beheaded, we will not retreat. In urgent telegram, we are extremely eager and await orders. The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, bowing. (3) Telegram to the Municipal Government: To Mayor Wu of the Shanghai Municipal Government: The Japanese violence in Shanghai this time is actually a planned and organized step by the Japanese, not an accidental outbreak. This can be proven by the Japanese acts of violence against our country. The Japanese have not repented of their brutal acts, but have dared to make unreasonable demands, even requesting our government to stop the anti-Japanese movement. Our colleagues in the association, witnessing this murderous and arsonist barbarity and unreasonable coercion, are filled with outrage. We believe that the national salvation movement is a legitimate action by the people of any country to protect their country and cannot be subdued by any force. We urge your Excellency to firmly reject the unreasonable demands of the Japanese and not be intimidated by their power in order to protect the spirit of national salvation. Our colleagues in the association are willing to serve as a backing until death. Urgent words may be poorly chosen, but we hope you will understand. The Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, bowing.

The Business Community's Anti-Japanese Association Begins to Form: The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, based on the resolution of the Extraordinary General Meeting of Members, organized the Shanghai Business Community Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association yesterday. Yesterday, it sent letters to the elected executive committee members, representatives of various industries, stating: "To the Honorable, This association convened an Extraordinary General Meeting of Members on the 20th of this month to discuss the organization of the Business Community Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. It was resolved that it should be organized, and 25 executive committee members were elected on the spot, with representatives of each industry responsible for handling matters. Your representative is also one of the elected executive committee members. We are sending a list of names and a letter for your information. According to the order of names at yesterday's election, Chen Zixiang, the representative of the North-South Goods Exchange Industry, ranked first, will be the convener. Please convene a meeting immediately to proceed. A combined statement."

Representatives of Stores on North Sichuan Road Requested Self-Defense from the Municipal Council Yesterday 149

Fei Xindun Expressed that There is No Need to Worry About Security

Representatives' Demands: The representatives sent to the Municipal Council yesterday were Wang Jian'e, Chen Jiufeng, and Xing Minyi. The original text of their demands is as follows: "Presenting a case regarding Japanese ruffians relying on violence to injure people and smash stores, requesting serious action. On January 20, five to six hundred Japanese ruffians suddenly appeared on North Sichuan Road, relying on violence to injure people without reason, disrupting public order, burning factories, and resisting arrest. The details have been reported in various newspapers. Our association is concerned and has a responsibility. Therefore, we convened a meeting on the 21st and resolved three points: (1) Please ask your president to be responsible for ordering the Japanese consulate to fulfill its obligations of punishing the perpetrators, paying compensation, and formally apologizing to the stores on this road. (2) If your president cannot maintain security, the militia organized by our association are all store employees, formal merchants, and have the same status as the International Volunteer Corps. We request your president to allow our militia to assist in patrols and allow us to provide our own firearms, and stores can also provide a handgun to prevent unforeseen events. All firearms should be exempt from consultation fees. Our association is willing to take full responsibility for any negligence. The above three points have been resolved by the meeting. In addition to submitting a formal letter, the meeting specially appointed representatives Wang Jian'e, Chen Jiufeng, and Xing Minyi to meet and seek instructions. We sincerely hope to be received and taught. Respectfully addressed to the President of the Municipal Council."

If necessary, the navy can also land. Therefore, there is no problem with the security of the concession. It is reported that Japanese residents will hold a general meeting in Peng Road tomorrow (i.e., today). The Municipal Council has also made full preparations and has sufficient military force to maintain order. Therefore, we hope that residents will not make a fuss." The representatives reiterated the losses suffered by the stores on North Sichuan Road due to the smashing of glass windows by the Japanese. Fei also agreed to inform the Japanese consul. There was no mention of self-defense and other issues.

The Social Bureau Prohibits New Year Holidays According to the Lunar Calendar 151

From February 1 to 10

And Specifies Two Punishment Measures

The Municipal Social Bureau issued a notice prohibiting closures under the pretext of the end of the lunar year. The notice states: "Notice is hereby given that closures and leaves of absence under the pretext of the end and beginning of the lunar year are not allowed. The bureau has issued notices prohibiting this in the past. Fearing that this will be ignored over time, we reiterate the prohibition and stipulate the following measures: (1) From February 1 to 10 of the Gregorian calendar, all commercial firms, companies, factories, and venues shall not take leave under the pretext of holidays. Violators will be ordered to pay double wages on a daily basis. (2) Workers and partners shall not take leave without authorization unless there are weddings, funerals, or serious illnesses. Violators will be fined double wages on a daily basis. If the leave exceeds ten days and affects business, they will be allowed to be dismissed. The above measures are announced to the public. All employers and employees in this city shall comply without fail. This notice is hereby given."
